Processing New Row [nil, nil, "66-year-old woman, who required an abdominal and perineal resection of the rectum with permanent colostomy at the James Cancer Hospital by Dr. John Winston about 15 years ago. \u00A0This is one of a couple of hospital admissions for acute onset bowel obstruction. \u00A0She presented to that Diley Ridge Medical Center Emergency Room, where imaging with a CAT scan confirmed a transition point in the lower midline of the pelvis between larger dilated proximal small bowel and decompressed distal small bowel. \u00A0A nasogastric tube was placed and she was transferred per her request to Mount Carmel West Hospital, where the rooms are all private. \u00A0She continued on gut rest with intravenous fluid rehydration and nasogastric tube decompression. \u00A0On the 18th, her nasogastric tube was clamped and she was allowed to have sips of clear liquids because her abdominal plain films were consistent with resolving obstruction. \u00A0On 02/19/2017, she was noted to have colostomy output and her diet was advanced to full liquids for 1 meal and solid foods thereafter. \u00A0Her nasogastric tube was removed on that morning. \u00A0At the time of her discharge, she had tolerated 2 solid food meals without vomiting or abdominal distension. \u00A0Her colostomy was functioning. \u00A0She had some mild diffuse abdominal soreness, but no pain requiring any type of analgesic. \u00A0Her nausea had completely resolved and never recurred.", nil, nil]
Initial Row Type Indicator = Note Detail
Row[2] = 66-year-old woman, who required an abdominal and perineal resection of the rectum with permanent colostomy at the James Cancer Hospital by Dr. John Winston about 15 years ago.  This is one of a couple of hospital admissions for acute onset bowel obstruction.  She presented to that Diley Ridge Medical Center Emergency Room, where imaging with a CAT scan confirmed a transition point in the lower midline of the pelvis between larger dilated proximal small bowel and decompressed distal small bowel.  A nasogastric tube was placed and she was transferred per her request to Mount Carmel West Hospital, where the rooms are all private.  She continued on gut rest with intravenous fluid rehydration and nasogastric tube decompression.  On the 18th, her nasogastric tube was clamped and she was allowed to have sips of clear liquids because her abdominal plain films were consistent with resolving obstruction.  On 02/19/2017, she was noted to have colostomy output and her diet was advanced to full liquids for 1 meal and solid foods thereafter.  Her nasogastric tube was removed on that morning.  At the time of her discharge, she had tolerated 2 solid food meals without vomiting or abdominal distension.  Her colostomy was functioning.  She had some mild diffuse abdominal soreness, but no pain requiring any type of analgesic.  Her nausea had completely resolved and never recurred.
